text:
If you leave out the packaged taco seasoning packet, and just bump up your other seasonings, & with about a 1/2 teaspoon of cornstarch for thickening, you will avoid the saltiness (plus the additives & preservatives) of the pre packaged and it is great.  Add onion or whatever other spices you like in your tacos or burritos.  Tasty.

The best way to shred this is to put the chicken in the crockpot. I used 3 frozen chicken breasts. Mixed all of the ingredients(decreased the taco seasoning and cumin per the reviews) and poured it over the chicken. I I cooked it for about 3 1/2 hours. This is the mexican version of the Zesty Slow Cooer Chicken Barbeque. You can make changes anyway and I don't think you could screw it up. Simple and good.

text:
I put my frozen chicken in the crock pot and covered it with plenty of enchilada sauce(out of tomato sauce) and then the salsa and other seasonings.  I use my own taco seasonings I make (taco seasoning I) which works wonderfully because you control the amount of salt.  Other than the enchilada sauce, I followed the recipe.  Cooked the frozen chicken on hi for 4 hours, then it turned to warm until I got home.  I shredded the chicken, wrapped it in tortillas, sprinkled with cheese and then poured the left over sauce from the crock pot over the enchiladas...nothing was wasted.  Good...Quick...Easy!

text:
Excellent!  I used the 'Taco Seasoning I' recipe (on this site) instead of the store packet, and omitted the cumin and chili (it's already in the seasoning).  Mixed this with the tomatoe sauce and salsa and poured it onto the chicken in a slow cooker.  After shredding the meat, I added a can of refried beans and heated that through in the slow cooker.  Put mixture in large burrito style shells, added tomatoe, some more salsa, and cheddar cheese.  Wrapped 5 of these and placed in 9 x 13 baking pan, topped with enchilada sauce, green onions, monterey jack and cheddar cheese.  Baked at 375F for about 15 minutes, and voila!

text:
I used 3 large frozen boneless chicken breasts, cooked in crockpot for 4 hours on high.  I used the taco seasoning recipe from this site and added a can of Rotel tomatoes (partially drained).  Once chicken was done, I took it out and shreaded it.  I put about 1/4 cup of liquid back into chicken and mixed it up.  Then I took the remaining liquid and pureed it.  Cooked pureed mixture on stove top with a pinch of cocoa and a pinch of garlic powder and a little corn starch to thicken it.  Then I put chicken mixture and cheese in flour tortillas and rolled up, put in pan, poured sauce on top and sprinkled cheese on top, put in oven till cheese was melted.  My family loved it and fought over the last one!

text:
I put 2 chicken breasts, 1/2 cup salsa, 8oz tomato sauce, a can of nonfat refried beans, and Taco Seasoning I (recommended from the site) in a crock pot for 4hrs on high, w/ med/low setting for the last hr. Shredded the chicken 2-3 hours in.

Initial verdict after 2 hrs: Too much taco seasoning as written (I stupidly left it at the 10 servings level). Next time I'd decrease to 4. The chili flavor was too strong. I'm noticing other reviewers included an extra chicken breast (3 for 4 servings) so that probably helped keep the seasoning from being too strong. The spices are overwhelming, especially the chili powder. I added 1 cup of cheese and bumped up the salsa to 1 cup but it still didn't mitigate the overpowering taste. 

Verdict after 4.5 hours of cooking in the crock pot: WOW the flavors really do need time to blend together and the spices aren't as overpowering after they've cooked for awhile. What a difference from the initial taste! Next time, I'll use 1/2 the Taco Season I ('cause it was still a little salty & the chili flavor was still kind of strong) and add 1/2 - 1 cup more of cheese. I might also try adding an extra chicken breast. Also, use burrito-size tortillas or they're too small and the filling bursts out! I learned my lesson the hard way :)

This was enough filling for 10 8 inch & 1 burrito size tortillas. All in all, this was SUPEReasy to make in the crock pot. It was my first time using it and I'm a believer now! :)

text:
When I hit the review button, a review I'd already done came up.  I didn't realize I'd made this before... and gave it a 5 the last time too. :-)  I made the filling as is, and did not think it too salty or spicy, and in fact, think that leaving out that much taco seasoning would make it bland.  I used it to make enchiladas this time - it was enough to fill about 10 of the 6".  I tried to keep it simple by putting a little cheddar cheese inside the tortilla, baking and then adding some Jack cheese on top for the last few minutes.  A little more cheese and it would've been perfect - I don't think the filling needs much help from other ingredients.  I'd also like to try this as a taco or tostada filling.  As a note, mine had to cook way more than 20 minutes before it was done.  I don't know what that was about, but it just didn't seem to cook well just sitting in sauce like that.

text:
Ooh!  We really liked this.  Of course, being one with an inability to follow recipes verbatim, I made some (just a few!) modifications; some, per users suggestions; some, to get rid of ingredients I had on hand.  I put 3 frozen chicken breasts in a slow cooker, used an 11 oz can of tomato sauce instead of 4oz, added a can of Rotel (diced tomatoes with chilies)  and about 3/4 cups of chopped onions, and only added 1/2-3/4 of the packet of taco seasoning.  I also added about 3/4 cups of water.  Slow cooked on high for 3.5 hours.  I was able to break apart the chicken after 2.5 hours.  Served with a bit of cheese (Kraft Mexican Blend) and sour cream in a tortilla wrap (Ole Xtreme Wellness High Fiber Low Carb keeps the meal in the healthy-zone and still tastes good :).

P.S.  I cubed sweet potatoes, microwaved for about 9 minutes and added to the slow cooker with about 45 minutes left to go.  They made a great healthy side dish when served with some extra sauce.  So yummy!

text:
Delicious and Super Easy! 
Like most everyone else I cut the taco seasoning. I did 1/4-1/2 a packet of taco seasoning, garlic, and chili powder, I left out the cumin and hot sauce. I put frozen chicken in the crock pot and covered it with the mix on low for 8 hours and it shredded perfectly when I got home! I combined this with refried beans, rice, cheese, sour cream and it was so yummy! This will definitely be on my list to make often!

text:
While this recipe is a good starting point, a few alterations bring it through the roof. Skil the extra chili powder and add a little bit of oregano. Chili powder is usually a mixture of cayenne, oregano, garlic, cumin and salt. Taco seasoning tends to have many of these ingredients already, so to add more is a bit redundant and likely to make your dish too salty. I also added about 1/3 c chopped onion, 1/3 c diced tomato and 1/2 can of black beans. The kind of salsa wasn't specified, so I went with Pace Chunky. With these changes, it made THE best taco filling I've ever had. Basically, experiment! Try adding the kinds of things you normally associate with tacos, adjust the seasonings if you like things a little different.

text:
After reading other reviews, I modified a bit, just because I was in a bit of a hurry.  I used frozen, raw chicken tenders (about 6 to 8) and put them in a slow cooker.  I mixed a 10 oz can of green chili enchalada sauce, a 8 oz. can of tomato sauce, 1/2 cup salsa, 1/2 packet of taco seasoning, 1 tsp cumen, 1 tsp chili powder, a dash of garlic powder and a can of black beans, rinsed and drained in a bowl.  Poured it over the frozen chicken tenders and mixed it up a little.  Put the slow cooker on high for about 2 1/2 hours.  Chicken was done and very tender.  Then I shredded it a bit using the 2 fork method, but leaving it a bit chunky.  We scooped it into wheat tortilla shells and topped it with lettuce, tomato, sour cream, taco cheese and black olives.  VERY GOOD.  Took less then 10 minutes to throw everything together in the slow cooker, so it was super simple.  I used the chicken tenders because I knew they would cook faster than the chicken breasts.  Will definately be adding this one to our favorites and passing it on to others.

text:
This recipe is terrific!  After reading some of the other reviews I did make some changes.  I substituted a can of Rotel with Cilantro and Lime for the salsa and used cumin, chili powder, garlic and chipotle seasoning instead of the taco mix to cut back on the salt.  I cooked it all in a crock pot so the chicken shreds easily and added a can of black beans right at the end.  I served it on large wrap tortillas and sprinkled it with cheddar cheese just before rolling.  The only change I would make next time is to drain the Rotel before adding.  As it was, though, it made an incredibly wonderful spicy chicken stew!

text:
What a great recipe!  I know there are some who object to reviews that aren't based strictly on the original version, but I want to thank all those who are willing to attempt the recipe with minor adjustments and then share them so that people who DON'T LIKE to cook (like me) can still attempt something new with greater confidence.  Personally, I took the suggestions of many others and left out the taco seasoning but kept all the rest.  Then I followed the suggestion of one other cook to mix together the sauce ingredients first then test the sauce for how salty I perceived it to be (perfect, in this case).  Finally, I followed another's lead and baked it slow cooker-style at 250F for 2 hours (fortunately I had the time to do that), and the chicken turned out beautifully!  Next time, however, I think I'll try cooking the dish uncovered as the sauce had not reduced and made the final product too soupy for my liking, which speaks of my technique not the quality of the recipe.  I'd definitely rate this higher than 5 if I could!  Thanks, Jubeefish, for the original, and everyone else for their input!

text:
Pretty good. While tasty, I'm not sure I'd make this on a regular basis. This is great for those nights when you need something simple and fuss-free on the table - QUICK (I'll save this for those occasions)! I do agree that this would be MUCH better if slow cooked. I had to add a considerable amount of chicken broth several times thruout the cooking process in order to keep my chicken "moist" (even on the lowest heat setting, my chicken seemed quite dry). Slow cooking would eliminate this. NOTE: Don't omit the cumin / chili powder! Yes, both are spices found in traditional taco seasoning, but adding them (in ADDITION) to the taco spices only enhances the overall flavor, IMHO. Served "taco style" with all the fixins' - chopped scallion and tomato, shredded lettuce, sharp cheddar and sour cream. Mexican rice completed our meal. Thanks for sharing, JUBEEFISH! My husband ESPECIALLY thanks you (he's ALWAYS begging me to make tacos lol!). :-)

This is delicious!  I make it in the slow cooker on high for about four hours.  Then I pull the chicken apart with a fork and knife and leave it on low for another half hour or so.  I up the salsa to a full cup and also throw in a small onion - diced.  I serve it as a burrito with fresh diced tomatoes and sour cream.  Mexican or Spanish rice and corn on the side and you have a great meal.  It's even better the next day for lunch!

The original recipe was too salty due to the taco seasoning.  I made a few changes to the recipe and give the new and improved recipe 5 stars.  Instead of taco seasoning, I just used cayan pepper, cilantro, and crushed red pepper.  I also added half a 4 ounce can diced green chilies, green onion and white onion to the mix as well.  When rolling burritos I added black beans and green salsa Verde.  I followed what JUBEEFISH suggested and put in baking pan, poured salsa and cheese on top of the burritos.  I added olives and more green onion and bakes for 15 minutes on 350.  Topped with sour cream and served.  They were AMAZING.

text:
Very good base and have made it twice now.
1st attempt was uninspiring as I left out: 

#  1 teaspoon ground cumin
# 2 cloves garlic, minced
# 1 teaspoon chili powder
# hot sauce to taste

2nd attempt I followed everything except I used 1 clove of garlic for a double recipe as mexican food with too much garlic is an instant turnoff. 

Cannot help but think that this is missing that authentic grilled flavor that liquid smoke just won't cover. Next time I am going to omit some of the salsa and replace with my own base salsa enhanced with various roasted peppers and then spread the meat mixture thin in a pie tin in my electric water smoker for a few minutes to add that wow it is missing. 

Salsa and hot sauce quality will make or break this recipe.

3.5 stars, almost there!

This made a very good burrito filling with black beans, rice, sour cream ,and cheese. However, I did make several alterations. Overall, when used in a burrito this is one tasty dish.

text:
My husband kept saying "wow" as he ate this! I felt quite proud after making this recipe! 

I didn't have any salsa on hand, so I used 8oz of tomato paste and chopped up 1/4ea of a red, yellow, and green pepper, as well as an onion instead. I also added 1/4 cup of water chicken bouillon and about 1tsp of cornstarch. 

I cooked it in the pan as directed (not in a crock pot as some people did) and used only a bit of salt, pepper, garlic salt, and a taco seasoning packet. 

Served them inside tortillas that I warmed on the stove in a non-stick skillet, and let them warm in the oven covered by a moist paper towel. They came out soft and almost steamed! Much better than the microwave tortillas. 

I also served it with white rice cooked with some chicken boullion, along with shredded cheese and sour cream.

text:
Super easy and tasted great. I used all the ingredients but made the recipe even easier. I mixed the tomato sauce, salsa, taco seasoning, cumin, garlic, and chili powder together and poured it over three whole chicken breasts in a skillet.  I also added some chicken broth to add more liquid and make sure the chicken breasts were covered completely.  I put it on the stove, let the liquid come to a boil, then covered the skillet and turned the heat down to simmer for 15 minutes.  After 15 minutes, I cubed the chicken instead of shredding it.  Turned out great. This recipe will be a keeper.

text:
This was very good with some adjustments.  There really isn't enough tomato sauce to "bring to a boil" and cook the chicken in, so I poached the chicken in chicken stock first, then shredded it and continued with the recipe.  I then boiled, strained, and used the stock to make rice as a side dish.  I also felt that the whole amount of taco seasoning was going to be far too much, so I added to taste and skipped the additional cumin and chili powder as they are already in the seasoning blend I used (Taco Seasoning I).  I also snuck some black beans and corn kernels into the filling.  I did need to add more liquid (used chicken stock), though I didn't cook on too high of a heat.  Final product was tasty!  Made 4 servings for 3 people, served with sour cream, guacamole, rice, and refried beans and it was all gone!

I just boil the chicen with the water to reduce messy from sauce, then smash the boiled chicken with the side of knife before pulling. text:
Scratch the taco seasoning mix.  Adds too much msg and stuff.  Mix the sauce, cumin (to taste), garlic, red pepper powder(instead of the chili powder) and paprica. Taste the poach BEFORE adding the chicken and adjust as needed.  Put chicken into poach, and cook for at least 20 mins. When ready to flake, tear it and poach a bit more.  When the chicken is completely flaked, add salsa to taste.  I then place it into fresh tortillas, cover with remaining sauce and chicken and a layer of cheddar and monterey jack shredded and bake for 20 mins or until the cheese bubbles.  Makes a great enchilada.

text:
I made this last night for my family and following the advice of others, doubled it and cooked in my crockpot. I also used the taco seasoning I recipe from this site, and not knowing how much to use, started off with one Tablespoon of seasoning for 4 chicken breasts, but upon trying a few hours later, added the rest of the spice from the recipe.  I then spooned the burrito filling into large flour soft tortilla, put a little taco cheese on top and placed on a hot griddle to crisp up the tortillas.  Served with refried beans and a green salad.  Fabulous!  Two of my family members had to have some antacid in the night (they are prety wimpy - no one else complained that it was too spicy), but said it was worth it for these great burritos!

text:
This was JUST what I was looking for (perhaps half the taco mix might make it a bit less salty).  I used it to make chicken quesadillas.  Warm a flour tortilla in a large pan on med high, layer on some chicken mixture, green onions, tomatoes, banana peppers, finely shredded cheese and cover with a second tortilla.  Cook for a minute or two 'till lightly crisped and flip 'till cheese is melted inside.  Cut into four and serve with salsa and sour cream.  I am going to try with chicken thighs as they are cheaper.  Also going to try freezing for easy to prepare make ahead dinner.

Delicious!!! I made this tonight for the first time. The only changes I made were to use 3 skinless, boneless chicken breasts instead of 2 and an 8 ounce can of tomato sauce instead of 4 ounces. All other ingredients remained the same. Very flavorful and easy to prepare. First time I have shredded chicken for a recipe and I was very proud of the end result. Also, for this dinner I made the following recipes from this site: Refried Beans without the Refry (in crockpot overnight), Spanish Rice II (prepared stovetop and transferred to rice cooker) and Janet's Rich Banana Bread (in the oven while dinner was being prepared).

I couldn't make it like the directions so I really had to tweak it. I didn't have tomato sauce so I just boiled the chicken in water instead. When it was done, I shredded it and put it in the skillet with 2/3 c. of water. I chopped up red bell pepper and added it. That had to be the best thing I've ever made and it satisfied my Mexican craving with low calories. I have enough for another meal and I can't wait to eat leftovers!

This turned out to be one of the best shredded chicken recipes.  Definitely make this in the crock pot since that is really the only way the chicken will get so tender. text:
This was really good! I did make a few changes. I cut up chicken thighs and legs and since i didn't have any salsa, i used an eight oz can of tomato sauceand set it to boil. When it boiled, i added 1/4 cup of sofrito, 1/2 of the taco packet, 1 tablespoon cayenne pepper, 1/2 teaspoon of chili powder and the two minced garlic cloves. The cumin seemed like too much so i left it out. I covered the pot and simmered for 10 mins. I added half a can of drained black beans and covered for another five mins. I preheated the oven to 350 degrees and laid a burrito on the chopping board and filled it with chopped lettuce, diced tomato, cheddar and Mexican cheese and then the chicken mixture. I wrapped.ip up, sprinkled a little cheese on the tops and baked it for ten mins. I served it with a little sour cream and it was so delicious! My boyfriend said it was better than taco bell!

This is very similar to the recipe I've been using for shredded chicken taco filling for a long time. text:
Used 3 frozen chicken breasts, the homemade taco seasoning, 2 (8 oz) cans tomato sauce (next time try just one can), fresh chopped onion, 2 fresh chopped garlic, 1/2 jalapeo, omitted the hot pepper sauce, (left other ingredients the same) and threw everything in the crock pot on high for about an hour, then low about 3 hours. Felt the chicken was getting tough, so put it on warm another 2 hrs before shredding the chicken. Mixed it back in with the sauce and kept on warm until we ate it about another 2 hrs. Chicken wasnt tough at all, had a really good flavor! Maybe would use more fresh ingredients to fancy it up a bit, but as it was perfect for its simplicity and great leftovers! Made awesome burritos except for the extra sauce making it kinda runny.

This is pretty good, though now that I've made it a few times, I play with it more-first, I omit the tomato sauce and up the salsa to about 1/2 cup. I also make my own taco seasoning, so there is no salt. Honestly, I can't even tell you the amounts-just look on the back of the packaged stuff and mix those ingredients (sans salt) until it looks/smells good to you. The other thing to make it easier is I put it all in a crock pot (small size pot as is) with frozen chicken and let it go all day-the house smells good, and with a 1 yr old, it's an easy dinner. Great in burritos or on chips!

text:
Yummy!  We just finished dinner and my husband and I love mild mexican food, and this was a hit with BOTH of us!  I shredded 3 cooked chicken breasts and put them in the crockpot, then made the following changes:  I added 6 oz tomato sauce, 1/2 c. salsa, 1/2 pkg of taco seasoning, 1 tsp minced garlic and added, as the recipe calls for, 1 tsp each of chili powder and cumin.  I let it cook for 8 hours--my husband stirred it a few times throughout the day.  Since we aren't big eaters, but love great food, I filled 4 small taco-size flour tortillas and added cheddar cheese inside and also topped them with cheddar cheese, too.  I put them in a microwavable dish and cooked them long enough to melt the cheese.  Delicious!

country:

text:
For my first attempt at burritos, this turned out pretty good.  I combined three recipes from this site:  this one, taco seasoning I, and white cheese sauce.  For this, I used 3 chicken breasts, 8 oz tomato sauce (can you even buy 4 oz cans?), a little more than 1/4 cup salsa, and only half of a 1.25 oz batch of taco seasoning I - MINUS ALL SALT.  I only used salt in my initial light seasoning of the raw chicken, thinking I could add more, and then I never needed it.  I also made a whole 1.25 oz of the taco seasoning thinking I'd need it, and I only used about half.  What I'd recommend is just adding things a little at a time until you have it to the taste and consistency you like.  Like another reviewer, I added rice and black beans to the mix.  Then made the burritos with diced fresh tomatoes , a little cheese, and poured white cheese sauce (recipe also on this site) over the burritos.  Cilantro would've been great but my husband doesn't like it so I left it out.  We did sprinkle hot sauce on top of the final product.  3.5 stars.

I didn't really treat this as "burrito filling", but more of just a spicy chicken dish.  I chopped up the chicken into small pieces, so it would cook faster.  I also changed up the ingredients some. I used mushroom spaghetti sauce since that's all I had on hand. I only used 1 TBS of taco seasoning instead of the whole package.  No cumin because I didn't have any.  Since it dried out while cooking, instead of adding water, I used a bottle of Blue Moon beer. I added some fresh parsley. I also added 1 1/2 TBS of Old Bay seasoning, which I think gave it an additional kick.

I thought that this was very good.  I used a 3-breast pkg of chicken from the store along with an 8 oz can of tomato sauce and left the rest of the seasonings the same. The cilantro in the beans gives this a fresher flavor and cuts the saltiness a little.  I will make this again!

text:
This was a hit at our house! It was the perfect amount of spiciness for my husband and I. He even polished off the leftovers for breakfast the next morning! I spooned it into warmed tortillas along with sour cream and Mexican cheese and then broiled in the oven for about 5 minutes. I would also suggest combining all ingredients and bringing to a boil before adding the chicken, this way everything will be combined evenly. We were short on time so I only simmered for 10-15 minutes and it still turned out great.. any longer and the chicken would've been too dry. I will definitely be making this again!
